Father's Day
Today is a day that the American people celebrate as Father's Day, and you all know this well. Do you know how many years it has been since Father's Day was established in America? "It has been three years." Is it only three years? "No." You should keep that in mind. Today, Director Kim Sang-cheol of the training center, please find out how many years it has been. "Yes." Today, let's talk a bit about Father's Day. 

Human beings are born through heaven and come to this earth. 
Among fathers today, there are biological fathers, stepfathers, and adoptive fathers. Do we need all three types of fathers? No, we only need a father with one name. 

Before I begin, I want to ask those among the American members who come from unfortunate families, where their parents have separated or who have a stepfather or stepmother, to raise their hands. Put them down. 

Today, while anyone in America generally observes Father's Day, I want to talk about the Father's Day we observe internally in our Unification Church, rather than the external meaning that others generally celebrate. 

To be born as "I"… we all know that the existence of "I" originates from the father. It is through the father that "I" came into being and was born through the mother. Thus, in the East, it is said that the father gives the bones and the mother gives the flesh. 

Flesh, no matter how good it is, must attach according to the skeleton. From this, we can discover that we must inherit all the principled frameworks within the concept of the father. 

In this country, when we look at America, for the nation of America to be formed, there must be a traditional content that can constitute the people. However, this tradition does not manifest externally at first glance; it is hidden within the organization. Even when we look at our skeleton, it is not visible; it is the flesh that is visible. 

In Eastern thought or in general concepts, when we say "heaven," we refer to something high, symbolizing infinite personality. We know that "heaven" is not something we can see but symbolizes a certain traditional personality in the conceptual world. On the other hand, "earth" symbolizes the mother. The earth is a tangible object that we can actually see and feel. 

In other words, in the East, when we say "universe," we refer to heaven and earth. Heaven symbolizes the father, and earth symbolizes the mother. From this perspective, we see that human beings are born through heaven and come to this earth, just as we receive the skeleton from the father, with heaven being the internal aspect and earth being the external aspect from which we receive our bodies through the mother. 

That is why we say we must be born with a heavenly nature. We say that we have a heavenly nature. Then we say that we have a human nature. Following that, we say there is a habitual, formed personality. In the East, these three are mentioned. What does this mean? It means that heaven symbolizes the father, earth symbolizes the mother, and our lives symbolize personality. Therefore, in our lives, we must resemble all the qualities of the father, the qualities of the mother, and the living qualities of both the mother and father. 

Living through such historical connections is the existence of "I." Therefore, we conclude that "I must resemble my mother, I must resemble my father, and I must cultivate a habitual personality according to the traditions that my mother and father desire." From this perspective, we must understand that the origin of "I" did not begin from today but was born through this historical lineage. 

Human beings are born receiving the benefits of three parents. 
When we look at human beings themselves, we can see that they possess three essential qualities. My body comes from the earth. The body represents this land. Therefore, we can say that the earth is our first parent. We are born from the earth. Next, within me, there are my parents who gave me life. Finally, there is the heavenly parent. Therefore, you must understand that you are born receiving the benefits of three parents. 

When we look at people, there is the physical person, the mental person, and the spiritual person. The mind and spirit are different. From this, we can see that human beings are born through these three elements. In other words, we must understand that "I" is born as a comprehensive entity representing the three connections. Therefore, everything is structured in three stages. 

Look at your eyes. Even in your eyes, there are the white part, the blue part, and the black part. When you look at your eyebrows, there are three layers. When you look at your entire face, there are eyes, a nose, and a mouth. Even the nose has two holes connected as one. Everything is equipped with the number three. Here is one side, here is another side, and here is another side—three sides. Everything is structured in this circular manner.

Today, I will briefly talk about "The Path."  
When we talk about a path, we generally refer to the path that humans walk, but we must examine and think about the various contents of this path once again.  
Nothing can exist without going through a path.  
When we look at the path centered around you as individuals, of course, you will think of the paths you walk every day, but you will also think of the path to your hometown. There is also the path to school, the path to government offices, and the path of life itself.  
While there are these external paths, we can also discover that there are higher internal paths. There is the path to find the teacher, the path to meet the teacher; such paths exist. We can see that no relationship can be established without connecting through a path, whether it is with any existence or any object. We can understand that the path also connects to work. We can see that relationships between friends can also be connected through this path. If we look at it this way, there are paths of filial piety, paths of loyalty, paths of service, and all of them are paths. We know that these paths refer to channels through which relative relationships can connect.  
If America has a path it must take to the world, that too is a path. Furthermore, there is a path that the world must take.  
This path does not establish itself merely as a path; we can summarize it here as a process that connects a subject and an object, linking cause and effect. The orbit of the earth is called a path. In the solar system, there is a path that the solar system revolves around. We know that nothing can exist without going through a path.  
Meeting God is a short-term encounter, but the path we take afterward is eternal.  
When we see it this way, we say that there are both true paths and bad paths. We can say that. Here, we can discover the obvious fact that nothing can be accomplished without going through a path. From a religious perspective, the paths of Buddhism, Christianity, and Islam are all different.  
From this perspective, what would be the true path that life must take in this world? There must be a path where one can completely do what one must do with their hands, see everything one must see with their eyes, hear everything one must hear with their ears, speak completely, and act completely. All of these are paths.  
Then, should that path be one that is only traveled for a few years, or should it be a path that continues forever? Is it better for the path to be close or far? What do you think? Of course, in achieving two goals, it is better to take the shortest distance, but those who travel longer distances tend to be wealthier. A country that can travel a long distance becomes a wealthy country. The image also changes. Such a country is called a great country.  
Also, do you wish for your life to be short? Do you want life to be short? "No." Wishing for it to be short refers to the relationship between two intervals, but we must understand that there are many other paths where being close is not good. Therefore, what I want to say to you, who are members of the Unification Church, is what path we should take. We cannot avoid thinking about this issue.  
You say, "Unification Church members should pass through the individual, through the tribe, through the nation, through the world, and through heaven to return to God." That is a significant distance you are referring to. Then, you say to go through heaven to reach God. When viewed this way, does meeting God mean everything ends? Meeting God means there is still a path to take. The path of heart remains. We desire to meet God, but we want to meet Him in a short period. After meeting Him, we do not want a short path. We desire an eternal path. The purpose of meeting God for oneself is to wish for it to be short, but the purpose of two people seeking Him is to hope for a long path. That is how it becomes.  
Is there happiness on the path we take?  
Do we walk the path to be unhappy or to be happy? Anyone you ask will say they walk the path to be happy. While there is a good path, we can conclude that there is also a bad path. Therefore, if we have a path to seek God, a path where we can meet God quickly is a good path, and a path where we meet Him slowly is a bad path. The faster, the better; the slower, the worse. We can find this difference here.  
When you came here this morning, thinking, "Ah, I'm going to Belvedere," if you look at that distance, there are 200 people gathered here, but you cannot help but think they are all different. For example, some may have hurriedly run to come early, while others may have hurriedly come because they were late. Which is better? There are those who rushed to come early, and those who rushed to come quickly because they were late; in terms of value, the person who hurried to come early is more valuable. The distance is the same, but if someone came late and rushed, that is not good.  
We learned here that the good and bad of distance change based on these contents.  
What does it depend on? It depends on our attitude, on ourselves. Why is that? It is because being able to stay in front of a destination for a long time is evidence of having been there for a long time. It means there was a lot of time to be together. We can set a standard with that difference.  
In the end, the person who came quickly may have come, but they could not stay together for long. When we look at the issue of the relationship between the subject and the object, we can find that good and bad are determined here. The person who started coming at dawn can find a connection that they were together for a long time. However, the person who came late has a shorter distance to be together when viewed in terms of time. We must think about how to measure the relationship of good and evil from here.  
You also want to go quickly to good places. You want to see quickly and meet quickly. When you go to your destination, if you go because you like it, the whole will appear good, but if you go because you dislike it, the whole will appear bad. Therefore, the path you take because you like it feels far but is perceived as close, while the path you take because you dislike it feels close but is perceived as far. Do you understand? "Yes." From this perspective, when we say, "Let us Unification Church members go to the heavenly kingdom," if there is someone who goes happily, it may feel far but can be digested as being very close. However, for someone who goes reluctantly, it is far and distant.  
From that perspective, if we desire a path, what kind of person will the path desire? Will it desire someone who goes happily or someone who goes reluctantly? "Someone who goes happily." No matter how good the path is, if someone complains, "What kind of path is this?" they will not like it. The more so, they must like that path. Even if one takes a bad path, instead of saying, "This path, why is it bad!" they should say, "Ah, you are ugly! I will love and protect you. Just wait a little." If they can think and comfort while enduring, how much will that path appreciate it? Everything is like that, everything. Treating with joy is what everyone desires, but treating with reluctance makes everyone dislike it.  
From this, we can conclude that there is happiness on the path taken with joy, and all environments treated with joy become happy, but on the path taken with reluctance, everything becomes unhappy. Everything dislikes it. If everything dislikes it, that is unhappiness.  
You have now understood that you must walk the path with a good heart. If a student going to school dislikes going to school and thinks, "Oh, why is there no time?" while eating, saying, "Why do I have to eat this food?" that student will surely become a bad student. They will definitely fail. On the other hand, if a student eats breakfast thinking, "Ah, I am eating to go to school," enjoying the food and liking going to school and studying, that person will surely become an excellent student and a model student of that school.  
There are many young men and women here, and when you get married, the wife has her path, and the husband has his path. Should you walk that path smiling, or should you walk it feeling bad? (Laughter) You should not only be happy at the wedding. You must be happy throughout your life. If you do so, the relationship between the two will improve, and their home will be happy, the yard will be happy, and all environments will be happy. Therefore, the saying that heaven comes closer to such environments is theoretical. Heaven is within that. However, conversely, if you constantly show resentment and look down on each other, everyone will dislike it.  
When we think about this, which path is the best path, the path we desire the most? Is it not the path where we can live forever and be happy forever? What path is that? It is the path to heaven.  
The path to life is a good path, the path to heaven is a narrow path.  
Now, is the path to heaven a short and close path, or a long path, an easy path, or a difficult path? All of these are not attached with good adjectives but rather with bad adjectives. That is why the Bible says that the path to death is wide and large, and many enter it, but the path to life is extremely rugged and narrow, so few find it.  
Those who go to death may seem to be smiling and enjoying themselves at first, but they are going to death, while the path to life is a path of tears, but one should not walk it while crying. One must walk it joyfully. This is where the establishment of joy comes from. The path that leads to death is initially wide, but it gradually narrows, and in the end, it becomes narrow and even more rugged, while the path that leads to life is initially narrow and rugged but becomes wider as one goes. It is the opposite. It is exactly the opposite. Do you understand? "Yes." If you understand that, there is no problem.  
Just because it is rugged does not mean it will always be rugged. It is rugged but will widen, so we must discover that we cannot help but walk the rugged path joyfully. If it remains narrow, that is wrong, but it will definitely widen. A wise person knows that it will definitely widen, so no matter how difficult it is, they cannot help but walk with great hope and a joyful heart.  
The good path, the path to heaven, wishes to pass quickly, but the path to death says, "Oh, world, do not go. Do not go." The cases are different. Therefore, if you think there will be difficult things in the future, you must do everything now. You must know that those going to heaven cannot help but do so.

The longer it is hammered, the more famous it becomes. It is heated and then suddenly plunged into water. It is not gently placed; it is plunged in. It must explode. After that, it must be hammered again… That kind of play must happen a lot. Depending on how much you do that, it becomes the best sword. It is the same with you.

Do you want to have a personality like a famous sword? Will you become a bad sword, or will you become a famous and good sword? “A good sword.” It’s easy to say. Saying it is easy. **The Original World of Creation and the Fallen World**

Originally, good and evil should not stand in opposition, and such a fact should not exist; this was the original ideal of God’s creation. The origin of good must always start from good, go through the process of good, and bring about the results of good to establish an environment of good, which was God’s original intention. Nevertheless, the existence of evil arose, which is not part of God’s ideal. We know through principle that evil did not originate from God but began through humanity centered around Satan. Ultimately, we understand that the result of evil arose from the fact that it could not become one with the original owner and became one with another owner. Satan was originally an archangel who should have served God faithfully and could have cooperated in achieving the ideal of creation. Nevertheless, he became the enemy of God, and thus evil was formed.

We must understand how great an enemy Satan is. This Satan is the representative who has shattered God’s ideal and taken away the entirety of God.

Originally, Adam and Eve were to become the temple of God and the body of God, and by becoming one with God, the internal parent, they were to become the central existence of all humanity and the entire world of existence. Therefore, through Adam and Eve, God could live, and through Adam and Eve, love could finally be formed, and through Adam and Eve, the ideal could be realized. Only through Adam and Eve could heaven be formed. If this had been the case, God could have been our direct Father, our direct parent, and could have been the root. Thus, we humans could have been born through the body of God and inherited God’s bloodline.

If God is the vertical parent as the internal parent, then Adam and Eve, as the ancestors of humanity, are the horizontal parents. This vertical and horizontal parentage should have been determined by becoming one with God, but the fact that this was not achieved is a great catastrophe. If it had been so, you would not have had to think about issues like eternal life or whether God exists; you could know God and be within God.

Just as when your heart is joyful, your body is also joyful, and when your body is joyful, your heart is joyful, there can be dancing and singing when both can rejoice together. Laughter can arise. If the heart is not joyful, the body cannot be joyful no matter how hard it tries. Likewise, if the body is not joyful, the heart cannot be joyful. It is a relative relationship.

If you had not fallen and God could dwell among you, you would have the center of the whole present because the center of the whole would be present in you, and as a relative self, you could become one with the whole in all fields. How much joy could you have been in such a position? You cannot even imagine the standard of that joy. If this had been the case, you would have been able to experience God’s feelings toward the universe and all feelings toward the world. You would have known how to walk and how to live before being tempted.

When you see how the teacher treats you, it is the same as how God treats the teacher. Therefore, for you to become a leader in the future, you must take responsibility for such difficult issues and train externally and internally. You must understand that such tasks remain. Established churches only look at heaven, only focus on spiritual heaven, and deal with internal issues, but we must also train externally to build heaven on earth centered on spirit and body.  
A person's talents are limited. How many people fit into that? How many people fit into that? That is why I must play the game of fitting in. If it does not fit, I must make it fit. This is something that can only be done through experience, so you must understand that if you do not go through such an experience, you cannot become a true leader. Thus, when you become a leader, you will leave an eternal new tradition that earns the praise of heaven and respect before all the people in the organization you lead through these experiences.  
Therefore, you must prepare for that. You must realize that you cannot avoid any external or internal training. I hope you become aware of this. Do not think it is unpleasant. Do not think you cannot do it.  
If you have once resolved to become a leader, do it with your life.  
Let me give you an example. I believe that anyone who has no interest in any object can become a professional. A professional is not something else. It depends on how much you do it and how persistently you overcome and do it. There may be talent and intelligence, but you can achieve it by doing several times more than relying on talent or intelligence. You just need to do several times more.  
When I was a student, there was a person among my classmates. When he was taught at school, he memorized everything from morning to evening. At first, he had low grades in the class. However, by the time he graduated, he had top grades in the class. He was persistent and did more than others.
No matter how much of a genius you are, if you compare someone who reads once and remembers with someone who has a poor memory but reads for a whole day, the person who reads for a whole day tends to remember longer. In the end, when you ask who knows the most, it turns out to be the person who memorized everything from the beginning. Later, when they become seniors, everyone tends to ask that person who memorized everything. That person ends up in a position where they can represent the whole.

Looking at this, don’t think that you can’t become an instructor. You can. It depends on how many times more effort you put in. How much effort you put in, that’s what matters. Yesterday, I heard David here say, “Older people don’t think well, so…” When I heard that, I thought, “As the person in charge of the training center, I shouldn’t have such thoughts…” Have you ever thought beyond the desire to eat when you’re hungry? Have you ever thought beyond that?

The teacher's mindset is like this. Whatever it is, hold onto one thing, and even if you can’t do it, struggle with what you’ve decided to do for your whole life. Even if you can’t achieve it in your lifetime, holding onto it until death is seen as greater. Then, when God has something left to reward, to whom will He give that reward? It will be given to such a person.

If you have once decided, “I will become something,” hold onto it until the end, hold onto it. If you have once decided, “I will become a leader,” then do it with your life on the line. The teacher is currently doing three things. One, two, three, and regardless of how difficult it is, they are moving forward with interest in that aspect. So, understand that, and no matter what difficulties arise, I hope you will overcome them and become those who establish a good tradition in the Unification Church.

*
